Taxpayers Association Held Executive Committee Meeting Yesterday

Wang Xiaolai and Xu Jiying Elected as Chairman and Vice Chairman

Yuan Jinchu, Hu Fengxiang, and Wang Yansong Appointed as Executive Directors

The Chinese Taxpayers Association of the Shanghai International Settlement held its first meeting of the 10th Executive Committee at 4:00 PM yesterday. The following executive committee members were present: Xu Jiying, Wang Xiaolai, Hu Fengxiang, Lu Feibaihong, Chu Huiseng, Yuan Jinchu, Yu Hualong, Liu Hongyuan, Shen Tianxin, Yan Esheng, Li Bohan, Wang Hanliang, Shi Liangcai, Cao Zhigong, Jin Runxiang, Zhang Yichen, Wang Yansong, Qian Chengxu, Zhang Henghai, Xu Yongyao Ting, Dong Zhenlong, and Wu Zhihao, totaling 23 members. Also present were Chinese Directors Yu Qiaqing and Committee Members Lin Kanghou and Chen Tingrui, as well as alternate Executive Committee Members Wang Weiying, Chen Jicheng, and Pei Yunqing. Wang Xiaolai was nominated as temporary chairman, and Secretary Tao Leqin recorded the minutes. After performing the formalities, the election of the chairman, vice chairman, and executive directors for this session began. The chairman first appointed Yu Hualong and Hu Fengxiang as vote counters and announcers. Twenty-three executive committee members were present, and after the voting, the results were announced. Wang Xiaolai received 20 votes and was elected as chairman. Xu Jiying received 20 votes and was elected as vice chairman. Yuan Jinchu received 20 votes, Hu Fengxiang received 18 votes, and Wang Yansong received 12 votes, and were all elected as executive directors. The secretary then reported on the resolutions of the last meeting of the 9th Executive Committee and other correspondence. The following cases were then discussed: A. Discussion on the resolution from the Delegates Assembly regarding the collection of municipal general donations by the Public Works Department, stating that the estimated rent should not be used as the standard for collecting general donations, except for self-produced and self-used properties. Resolved: To send a letter to the Public Works Department and the Chinese Affairs Office to handle the matter. B. Discussion on the resolution from the Delegates Assembly regarding reducing hawker license fees and addressing abuses of hawkers by the police. Resolved: To send a letter to the Public Works Department and the relevant Chinese committee members to handle the matter. C. Discussion on the request from the China National Products United Bazaar to transfer a letter to the Public Works Department requesting exemption from taxes and the issuance of a license for the Shanghai Poor People's Capital Lending First Generation Office. Resolved: To instruct the executive directors to consult with the Chinese Directors to discuss progress. D. Discussion on the proposal that the Public Works Department should issue advance notices when collecting quarterly donations, allowing 14 days for payment, to avoid residents being treated unfairly due to insufficient notice. Resolved: To send a letter to the Public Works Department stating that notices should be issued in advance before collecting donations to allow residents to prepare, and that the attitude of the collection staff should be improved to prevent arbitrary yelling. E. Discussion on the letter from the Hulin Company regarding order negotiations. Resolved: To handle the matter separately. F. Discussion on the letter from Cao Yingjun regarding the Racecourse's refusal to allow Chinese people to enter. Resolved: To instruct the executive directors to investigate the details and then negotiate. G. Chu Huiseng proposed that a letter be sent to the Public Works Department stating that the Chinese Directors should strive to increase the number of Chinese committee members on each committee. Resolved: Passed. To request the Chinese Directors to strive for this when attending meetings.

Dachang Steamer Sinks

Off Wusongkou Last Night

Collided with Dahu Steamer

The Dachang steamer of the Shanghai Dahu Company, coming to Shanghai from Dapu, Haizhou, last night at 8:30 PM, when eight nautical miles away from the Wusongkou, the Dahu Steamer of the Pingan Company was sailing out of Wusongkou, and somehow collided with the Dachang steamer. The Dachang steamer was damaged on the port side, in the engine room, and was penetrated. Seawater immediately flooded in and the ship gradually sank. By 10:00 PM, it had completely sunk, with only the mast visible. Of the over 100 passengers and crew members, over 70 were rescued by the Dahu steamer. However, the comprador Pang, carter He Shengcai, carter Cai, carter Wang Pingsheng, carpenter Pi Gen, sailor A Fa, and seven stokers are currently missing. The Dahu steamer was undamaged and sailed into Wusong, where it anchored.

American Ambassador Arrives in Shanghai Today

Accompanied by Rear Admiral Mark L. Bristol

According to the American Evening Post, American Ambassador Johnson will arrive in Shanghai from Beijing aboard the American warship Houston, accompanied by Rear Admiral Mark L. Bristol, Commander-in-Chief of the Asiatic Fleet, and is expected to arrive early tomorrow morning (the 15th). The American Ambassador has been in Beijing for two months and has met with Foreign Minister Wang and others multiple times to discuss the extraterritoriality issue. During his stay in Shanghai, he will stay at the Cathay Hotel. Rear Admiral Bristol traveled directly to the capital aboard the warship from Manila a week ago, visiting the National Government according to international protocol, and is now coming to Shanghai. The warship will be moored between buoys 10 and 11 on the Huangpu River and is expected to stay in Shanghai for several weeks before heading north to Qingdao and Yantai for the summer.

Yarn Transportation Resumes Yesterday

Ships Load and Transport for Export

The strike by customs declaration workers in Shanghai halted the transportation of cotton cloth and yarn. Since the cotton yarn portion of the industry resumed transportation, merchants have been rushing to load goods for export. The various circumstances yesterday are recorded as follows:

Yarn Transportation Resumes　After the customs declaration industry workers partially resumed work yesterday, the Haichang Company's ship, the Hai Shun, bound for Yingkou, the China Merchants Bureau's ship, the Guangli, bound for Fuzhou, and various companies' ships bound for Chongqing, Tianjin, Qingdao, and other destinations, were all fully loaded with cotton yarn for export yesterday, totaling over 5,000 pieces. Local guest merchants, hearing news of the resumption of work in the cotton yarn department of the customs declaration workers, purchased cotton yarn in large quantities in order to ship it out today because the General Taxation Department is implementing the cancellation of the cotton yarn and cloth export permits after April 15 and will be collecting new taxes according to regulations.

Group Leaders Meeting　The Customs Declaration Industry Union held a meeting of group leaders at 3:00 PM yesterday. Present were the leader and deputy leaders of the Hankou group, Chen Songqing and others, Shi Baoshan of the Yantai group, Chuan Yunwu of the Yingkou group, Gu Zongyue of the Tianjin group, and over 20 other group leaders. Fang Heping, director of the union, and the chairman reported on the situation at the Social Affairs Bureau on the 13th. The issue of cotton cloth transportation fees will be first discussed by Shi Zhikun and others of the Customs Declaration Association together with Chen Songyuan, Deng Zhonghe, and other representatives of the Cotton Cloth Industry Association, and then submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau for handling. It was also resolved that the cotton yarn portion of the industry has resumed work, but unless the cotton cloth portion is adequately resolved, a second step will be taken. If necessary, unified action will be taken for all goods, including foreign goods, miscellaneous goods, and cotton yarn.

Chen Shaokuan Arrives in Shanghai for Discussions

Yang Shuzhuang Expected to Arrive in Shanghai at the End of the Month

Naval Review is an Annual Event

According to the Guowen News Agency, Chen Shaokuan, Acting Minister of the Navy and Director of the Jiangnan Shipyard, arrived in Shanghai from Beijing yesterday morning. When interviewed by reporters at the shipyard, he stated: (1) Minister Yang (Shuzhuang) is expected to arrive in Shanghai at the end of the month as the National Assembly is about to open. Director Li (Shijia) went to Fujian to report on naval affairs and returned to Shanghai on the Wuxiang commercial ship today. (2) Lin Zhong and others are still being detained in Beijing. Whether Lin and others are suspected of involvement in the June 1st coup is being handled by the Central Committee. The Navy has no specific opinion. Moreover, Lin and others left the Navy after the coup. The telegrams sent by the ship captains this time were simply personal requests to Minister Yang. (3) The naval review is an annual event, not a special event. The reviewing officers are all directors of the ministry, including Li Shijia, Director of the General Affairs Department, Yang Qingzhen, Director of the Military Balance Department, Lin Xianxin, Director of the Ordnance Department, Tang Dexin, Director of the Naval Affairs Department, Xu Weixiang, Director of the Maritime Affairs Department, Luo Xuhe, Director of the Management Department, and Major General Counselor Ren Guangzi. The review location is in the capital. The review procedure generally involves transferring mobile ships to Beijing in batches for inspection. For those that cannot be moved, such as the Naval Academy in Mawei, review officers will be sent to inspect them at a scheduled time. The review is expected to last about three to four weeks. (4) The conflict with the China Merchants Electric Tramway Company will be mediated by Mayor Zhang, who will presumably have a solution. However, the specific steps have not yet been decided. (5) The Minsheng warship is scheduled to be launched on May 5. Construction of subsequent ships is also being planned. As for the previously rumored order for a 2,000-ton gunboat from Japan, as it requires over 4 million in funding, methods of raising funds and negotiating credit terms are currently being discussed, and bidding may soon be used to make a decision.

Hu Zuyu Arrives in Shanghai

Seeking Treatment for Leg Ailment

Also Visiting the Wounded Commander

Xiong Shihui, Commander of the Songhu Garrison, has resigned from his position as Commander of the 5th Division, and his position has been filled by Hu Zuyu, the deputy commander. According to Director Li Dezhao of the Garrison Headquarters yesterday, when Commander Xiong was injured in the plane crash, Hu originally intended to come to Shanghai to visit him, but was unable to leave due to leading troops in suppressing bandits in eastern Jiangxi. Currently, Deputy Commander Zhou Hunyuan has gone to the front lines (Nanchang). Hu plans to take this opportunity to come to Shanghai, visit Commander Xiong, and seek a good doctor to treat his leg ailment. Four years ago, the area around the knee of Hu's right leg suddenly swelled and became painful, making it difficult for him to move. He took traditional Chinese medicine for two months before being able to walk, but still felt strained and sore when sitting or standing, and found it difficult to bend freely and inconvenient to ride a horse. Recently, he noticed that his right leg was thinner, with a circumference about an inch smaller than his left leg. Doctors advised him to take Guanzhong Velvet Antler, but it was ineffective. Yesterday, he telegraphed me (Li referring to himself), asking me to place an advertisement seeking a good doctor. Anyone who can provide information on the cause and treatment of the ailment should send it to the Garrison Headquarters (Li Dezhao) and I will forward it. Whether in Shanghai or elsewhere, Hu will go for treatment. Also, Commander Xiong's leg injury is gradually recovering, and he can now walk slightly without using a cane.

Zhu Tingqi Went to Beijing Last Night

To Request Instructions on Taking Over the Smuggling Prevention Bureau

The Smuggling Prevention Department of the Ministry of Finance has been ordered to be abolished. All national salt smuggling prevention bureaus will be directly under the jurisdiction of the Salt Affairs Inspection Office, and a tax police section will be added to the office to oversee these matters. Zhu Tingqi, the director of the office, took the overnight express train to Beijing last night to request instructions on establishing the section and taking over the bureaus.

Farewell Celebration for Liu Weichi by Staff of Two Railways

Liu Weichi, Director of the Business Department of the Ministry of Railways, has been appointed as the Chairman of the Pinghan Railway Reorganization Committee. The staff of the two railways, recognizing that Mr. Liu's term, though only one year, has been considerate to the employees, held a farewell dinner at Xinghua Lou the night before last, expressing their sentiments of parting and welcoming the new Director Luo Xin and the new Chief of General Affairs, Mr. Hu. Deputy Director Zheng Baozhao, Chief of the two railway sections, Chen Xinghan, Chief of the Jinghu railway section, Chen Zhongying, and representatives of the special party branch, Min Luoyu, gave farewell speeches in succession. Mr. Liu, Mr. Luo, and Mr. Hu responded, generally offering mutual encouragement. The hosts and guests enjoyed themselves until 10:00 PM before dispersing. Mr. Liu departed by night train at 11:30 PM last night. He will make a brief stay in Beijing before traveling up the river to Wuhan to assume his new position. Besides posting farewell banners at the North Station, more than a hundred colleagues from the two railways went to the station to see him off, including Director Luo Xin, Liu Chengchang, Zheng Baozhao, the two Chiefs, Chen Zhongying, Chen Xinghan, and other section chiefs and colleagues. Mr. Liu shook hands with everyone to bid farewell. The workers also prepared military music and firecrackers, which were set off along the way as the train departed. Mr. Liu sped away amidst the military music and firecrackers.

U.S. National Foreign Trade Convention Scheduled

This Session to be Held in New York

Message from the U.S. Department of Commerce

The National News Agency reports that the U.S. Commercial Counselor's Office in Shanghai has received a telegram from the National Foreign Trade Council in New York, stating that the 18th National Foreign Trade Convention is scheduled for May 28th and 29th in New York. The Council has been established for seventeen years, and this is the first time the annual meeting is being held in New York. New York occupies an important position in foreign trade, so it is expected that this year's convention will have more participants than in previous years. The Council's Chairman, Mr. Farrell, stated in a document announcing the convening of the convention at the Commodore Hotel in New York that this session will be a good opportunity to thoroughly study the economic conditions and operations in overseas trade. The downturn in world commerce is gradually showing signs of abating, so the turning point is imminent. It is predicted that the number of representatives from the Far East attending this time will be particularly large. All representatives participating in the convention must first remit ten U.S. dollars to the Secretary of the National Foreign Trade Council in New York City as a registration fee.

Japan's Trade with China in Three Months

Excess of Exports Over Imports: 6 Million Yuan

The Japanese Commercial Counselor in Shanghai received a telegram from Tokyo stating that in March of this year, Japan's export trade was worth 96 million Japanese yen, resulting in an excess of imports over exports of 31 million yen. From January of this year, the export trade in the three months totaled 293 million yen, a decrease of 107 million yen compared to the same period last year. However, due to the reduction in imported raw materials, the total excess of imports over exports in the three months was only 37 million yen. In March of this year, exports to China were worth 23 million yen, so the excess of exports over imports was 5 million yen. In the three months of this year, the total excess of exports over imports in trade with China was 6 million yuan, a decrease of 20 million yuan compared to the same period last year.

Customs Notice: Two Tax Rates

To be Implemented Starting This Month, 8th

Mei Weiliang, Commissioner of Customs of the Jianghai Customs, issued a notice yesterday, stating: "Notice is hereby given that, upon investigation, the tax rates for imported raw materials for straw hats and exported bamboo poles have now been stipulated as follows, by order of the Inspector General of Customs, forwarded by the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance: A. Tax rates for imported raw materials for straw hats: (1) Gold thread grass shall be taxed according to item A of No. 564 of the new tariff (wheat straw, Panama grass, etc., and their products), at 10% ad valorem; (2) Glass grass shall be taxed according to No. 647 of the new tariff (unlisted goods), at 12.5% ad valorem; (3) Hemp grass shall be taxed according to No. 73 of the new tariff (flax, ramie, hemp), at 5% ad valorem; (4) Paper grass shall be taxed according to No. 526 of the new tariff (unlisted paper goods and goods made of paper), at 15% ad valorem. B. Tax rates for exported bamboo poles: (1) Bamboo poles with a diameter exceeding one inch shall be taxed at the current export tariff rate of 5 fen of silver per thousand poles for the regular tax and 2.5 fen of silver for the surtax; (2) Bamboo poles with a diameter not exceeding one inch shall be taxed by weight, at 1.12 li of silver per hundred catties for the regular tax and 0.56 li of silver for the surtax. All of the above tax rates shall be uniformly implemented starting from the 8th of this month. Let all merchants be fully aware of this. This notice is hereby given."

Native Cloth Industry Requests Tax Exemption for Sales Abroad

Since submitting a request to the National Government and the Ministry of Finance for tax exemption and transportation permits, the Native Cloth Industry Association in Shanghai has received approval from the Ministry of Finance to issue them. However, the association yesterday reported that the Shanghai Jianghai Customs is still levying customs duties on goods transported to the South Seas Islands, Hong Kong, Dalian, Andong, and other areas where unified taxes have not been implemented, causing renewed anxiety among native cloth merchants. Therefore, they have once again petitioned the Ministry of Finance, requesting that it instruct the National Customs Administration to order the customs and tax authorities not to create difficulties in order to alleviate the hardships of merchants. The reasons stated are: (1) The customs authorities consider the transportation of goods to Hong Kong, the South Seas Islands, Dalian, Yingkou, Andong, and Weihaiwei as exports, and therefore levy taxes. They are unaware that this native cloth is entirely purchased and used by patriotic overseas Chinese. Merchants are taking advantage of opportunities to reduce costs, with a long-term vision of hoping to regain rights. If imported taxes are heavily levied when transporting goods to other foreign countries, it is hoped that our government will do its best to protect them. How can we levy taxes again when the opportunity to promote exports is ripe and exemptions have been granted? This is something that should be considered. (2) Artificial handloom households are scattered in rural areas, and yarn is purchased piecemeal. How can they obtain unified tax certificates? However, they are entirely cotton fabrics directly woven after the unified tax has been paid, which can prove that there is no taking advantage of loopholes or false pretenses. A detailed study shows that the tax has already been obtained at the root. This is something that should be considered. (3) In the old days, there were numerous customs barriers, and transit taxes were always regarded as multiple taxes. However, this artificial hand-woven cloth only paid one or two wen per bolt when transported from Songjiang and Taicang to Shanghai. After completing one passage, it could reach Xiamen directly. After the prevalence of foreign goods, native cloth was almost completely taken over. The National Government decided to promote domestic goods and approved a national uniform tax exemption. As a result, the output of various provinces has increased many times over the past. It is implementing a one-item-one-tax policy. The government attaches great importance to people's livelihood. Before the association received the order from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, it followed the resolution of the National Government to regard hand-made native cloth as a major domestic product. The supply and demand sides are mostly poor people. In order to promote domestic goods and maintain people's livelihood, based on the case of the 7th year of the Republic, a general tax exemption was ordered in accordance with the standard six rules to promote sales. The taxation agency has no power to change the established case of general tax exemption. This is something that should be maintained.

Egg Export Trade Will Fail

United States Implements Increased Taxes

According to news from the egg industry in Shanghai, the much-publicized U.S. tax increase bill will be implemented on the 16th of this month. Hongkou Three Silk Weaving Factories Resumed Work Yesterday

Xiehua Resolved Through Coordination and Mediation

Yuhua Both Sides Insist

The workers of Xiehua, Yuhua, Fenghua, and other yarn weaving factories in the Hongkou District went on strike together on the 11th to oppose the wage reductions at the Xiehua and Yuhua factories. After the Social Affairs Bureau's persuasion, they all returned to work in the factories yesterday morning. The situation yesterday is recorded separately below:

Xiehua Resolved: The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau convened a mediation committee at 2:00 PM yesterday to conduct mediation. Representatives of the capital side, Chen Yunming and Zhang Zhaoqing, and representatives of the labor side, Ni Longsheng and Wei Shouchang, attended. Chairman Zhu Guilin and Recorder Wang Zhichin were present. After a long discussion, an agreement was signed: (1) The labor and capital sides voluntarily withdrew the wage reduction dispute; (2) The factory voluntarily closes down and will clear the raw materials from today, ending within 20 days; (3) The existing warps are to be distributed equally to union members and non-members; (4) During this clearing period, the union is fully responsible for the work of union members.

Yuhua Undecided: The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau convened a questioning session at 1:00 PM yesterday. Representatives of both labor and capital sides attended on time. Zhu Guilin was the chairman, and Wang Zhichin was the recorder. The labor side argued that the wage of three li and three mills per foot was decided by the Municipal Government's arbitration, so it must be based on this regulation. The capital side argued that silk weaving factories with smaller scales in the Hongkou area only pay two li and eight mills, so they insisted on not agreeing. The chairman announced that the formal convening of mediation would be rescheduled.

Airmail Can Use Ordinary Stamps

Starting from the 16th

According to a message from the Shanghai Post Office, starting on the 16th of this month, airmail can use ordinary stamps. All previous restrictions requiring the exclusive use of airmail stamps will be canceled. However, the post office has specially manufactured an envelope, which will be sold at the windows of various post offices soon, specially for mailing airmail letters. The envelope is printed in the Western style, 11 cm high and 15 cm wide. The front is printed with two horizontal and two vertical straight lines in dark blue. Above the horizontal and vertical lines, space is reserved for affixing postage stamps. The word "Aviation" is printed between the two lines. To the left of the straight line, the words "(Airmail)" are printed. If the public uses its own envelope, if the design matches this regulation, it can also be used. If Chinese old-style envelopes are used, two black lines should be added to the top of the envelope in ink. The distance between the black lines and the top of the envelope should be about one-fifth of the total length of the envelope. Within that space, the words "(Airmail)" should be written. As for postcards, printed matter, and parcels, the wrapping should also be handled in this way. If these regulations are not followed, causing the item that should have been delivered by airmail to be sent by ordinary mail, the post office will not be responsible. Starting on the same day, the airmail postage payable on all airmail parcels will still be charged at 15 cents per item per 20 cm of weight, or any fraction thereof, for every 1,000 kilometers of travel. The style of the specially made airmail envelope can be seen on the notices at various post offices.

Bai Zhiying's Drug Trafficking is a False Accusation

Report of the Party Department's Investigation

The National News Agency reports that Ms. Bai Zhiying, an employee of the executive director of the China National Drug Prevention Association, Huang Jiahuishi, was discovered to be transporting morphine by Hong Kong Customs. The news spread, and all circles are paying close attention. The 18th Sub-department of the Third District of this city, because Huang Jiahuishi is a probationary party member of this sub-department, bears the responsibility and must investigate the truth in detail in order to properly deal with it. At the 29th party member congress, it was decided to send four comrades to investigate. According to the detailed report of the sub-department's investigators, it is believed that the case is entirely a false accusation, and there are documents that can be used to corroborate it. The investigation report is recorded below for public evaluation. It is found that Mr. Huang has devoted himself to the drug prevention movement for eight years. In the course of the work, it is inevitable that he will offend all parties. The enemy's conspiracy was expected long ago. Recently, he has been particularly active in protesting the monopoly of opium sales. This time, he left Shanghai to inspect the situation of tobacco prohibition in Taiwan. Because he knew the deterioration of the situation, he kept it a secret beforehand. At that time, someone visited Mr. Huang, and his family replied that he had gone to Hong Kong. Unexpectedly, two days after he left Shanghai, there was news of this matter. It is found that the passport shown by Mr. Huang clearly bears the seal of the Keelung Police Department as proof. The date of arrival and departure can be checked. After Mr. Huang stayed in Taiwan for a week, he left Taiwan and went to Xiamen. Unexpectedly, after arriving in Xiamen, he learned that he had been falsely accused to the Central Government of transporting morphine. At the same time, a Xiamen local merchant colluded with his accomplices to board the ship, using assassination methods to prevent him from declaring his innocence. Unable to clear his name, Mr. Huang received assistance from a friend and temporarily avoided it in the Gulangyu Public Concession for a few days. It was not until March 29th that he took the Taiyuan Wheel back to Shanghai. He was escorted by drug prevention personnel from Xiamen before escaping the trap. With the assistance of various parties, Mr. Huang obtained documents and photos of a local merchant, surnamed Zhang, colluding with a certain doctor to conspire to frame him and his wife. There was also a letter from a certain female American drug prevention leader, Chen, about the opponent's conspiracy plan, advising Mr. Huang to be careful. After investigation and review, the documents can indeed prove the false accusation and will be disclosed and published one by one when necessary. In order to complete the Prime Minister's legacy of drug prevention, we do not want the entire drug prevention movement to be affected by the false accusations against Mr. and Mrs. Huang. Therefore, the truth of the investigation is announced to the public, and we respectfully ask for your evaluation.

Technician Certificate Renewal Deadline

Extended Another Six Months

Regarding the matter of extending the technician certificate renewal deadline by another six months, the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Works, the competent authority in this city, has already been ordered to issue a public announcement. Now, we have obtained the original text of the Shanghai Municipal Government's instruction to the Bureau of Public Works, which is transcribed below for compliance:

"By order:

The Executive Yuan's Instruction No. 1496 states:

Based on the report submitted by Kong Xiangxi, Minister of Industry, requesting leniency for those who have exceeded the deadline and for continued extension of the technician certificate renewal deadline for national compliance, according to Articles 13 and 14 of the Implementing Regulations for Technician Registration, those who obtained certificates before the implementation of the Technician Registration Law, according to the separate regulations for technician registration of various local governments, and those who passed the technician selection examination of the former Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce in Beijing, should apply to the competent ministry for the issuance of certificates within six months after the implementation of the new law.

The Technician Registration Law was promulgated and implemented on October 10, 1929. The deadline for applying for the issuance of the aforementioned registration certificates has been repeatedly extended by the former Ministries of Agriculture and Mining and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, with reasons stated and approved by the Executive Yuan, until the deadline of April 10 of this year, with a declaration that no further extensions would be granted, and this has been communicated for compliance.

Now, the above-mentioned extension deadline is approaching again. It is necessary to strictly follow the provisions of Article 16 of the Technician Registration Law and notify all provincial and municipal governments that those who have not registered by the deadline but are engaged in various technical affairs by delegation should be ordered to cease operations and be fined by the competent authorities to uphold the law.

However, the domestic reactionary forces were only recently subdued in the past few months. During the military operations, in provinces and regions affiliated with the reactionary forces, such as Shaanxi Province, which lacked a provincial government organization, official documents issued by the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce were returned unopened by the post office. In provinces such as Hebei and Shanxi, after receiving official documents, they were often shelved and ignored.

The former Ministry of Industry and Commerce, regarding Zhong Sensheng's application for technician registration, consulted the Peiping Municipal Government in April of last year to verify the documents, and only on February 17 of this year did it receive a reply regarding the verification, stating that it had been delayed due to the military situation and was only handled by the Bureau of Public Works in November of last year when clearing accumulated cases. The exchange of official documents took ten months.

Based on this, it can be inferred that the official documents issued by the Executive Yuan and the former ministry regarding the extension of the technician certificate renewal deadline were not followed, which was unavoidable due to the circumstances. Those who obtained certificates according to the separate technician registration regulations of the Peiping and Tianjin Municipal Governments, as well as those who hold registration certificates from other local governments or technician certificates from the former Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce's technician selection examination, who were engaged in business in provinces and regions within the sphere of reactionary forces, were unable to clearly understand the renewal deadline, causing delays. This is understandable.

Furthermore, technical personnel engaged in technical work in Hunan and Jiangxi provinces were even more unable to renew their certificates due to the widespread turmoil caused by the communist bandits. Their situation is particularly pitiable. As for other provinces and regions that were not affiliated with reactionary forces or severely ravaged by communist bandits, those who were registered and certified by local governments to engage in business were often graduates of secondary vocational schools or had no academic qualifications at all, relying solely on long-term experience to assess their service performance, which was sufficient for social needs and satisfactory. However, due to their academic qualifications not meeting the requirements of the Technician Registration Law, their applications for new certificates were often rejected. Before the expiration of the extension period, the government had not yet taken measures to ban their business operations. Once the deadline expires, they would have to cease operations immediately according to law. This would not only make it impossible for the technical personnel who were forced to cease operations to maintain their livelihoods but also cause a sudden shortage in social needs.

The previous approval was given to the Executive Yuan's Secretariat's official letter forwarding a joint petition from Gu Daosheng and others requesting relief, and the reasons stated were similar. After careful consideration, the Ministry is drafting relief measures to cope with the situation and take into account the facts. However, the extended deadline is approaching, and the procedures for submitting the draft for approval, promulgation, and compliance are unlikely to be completed before the deadline. Therefore, it seems necessary to extend the deadline to seek relief.

Based on the above-mentioned reasons, the Ministry requests leniency from the Executive Yuan to continue to order the extension of the deadline for issuing certificates for technicians registered with the former Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce and various local governments for six months to show the government's concern for the people's difficulties and demonstrate its leniency and generosity. Whether the reasons for requesting the extension of the deadline for issuing technician certificates previously registered with the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce and various local governments are appropriate is hereby submitted for review and implementation.

Based on this, the request is factual and should be approved as requested. In addition to reporting to the National Government for review and record-keeping and issuing a notice, the municipal government is ordered to inform and instruct its subordinates to take note. This order, etc., is hereby given.

Furthermore, the Ministry of Industry's telegram states: "The technician certificate renewal deadline has been submitted for approval. The extended deadline of six months will commence on April 10 of this year. Please instruct the competent authorities to issue a public announcement."

Based on this, the bureau is ordered to take note. This order, etc., is hereby given.

News from Trade Associations

The Ministry of Industry, in order to solicit information on the plight of industry and commerce, issued a circular to the entire country, which was published in this newspaper. It is now reported that the Shanghai Tailors' Association has submitted a letter to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, stating the plight of the industry and requesting assistance. The original letter reads as follows:

"Respectfully replying:

We received your letter dated [date] which opened with: 'By order: Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs Instruction No. 7044, for compliance. By order: Ministry of Industry Instruction Shangzi No. 1215, which states: 'In order to implement Xu Peihuang's proposal in the resolution of the National Industry and Commerce Conference, it is proposed that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce announce to the entire country that each industry and commerce should list its own hardships, collect them for study, and devise ways to provide relief. Furthermore, the proposal of Ju Jianyang, Director of the Hankou Commodity Inspection Bureau, is to instruct the chambers of commerce in various places to inform the various trades and guilds to state in detail their business difficulties or successes, as well as their hopes for government relief or assistance. The chambers of commerce should present them for discussion at each meeting to promote commercial development.'

The above matters have been approved at the conference, instructing us to list in detail the difficulties of our industry in order to facilitate review. Upon receiving this order, our association sent letters to various members to solicit information on their difficulties or successes. In response, the reported areas of suffering are briefly stated as follows:

1. The industry suffers from the weakness of domestic production capacity, which results in the need to import most of the required materials such as woolens, leading to an annual outflow of profits, which is immeasurable. Recently, the impact on our industry has been even greater due to the high cost of gold and low cost of silver. The government should devise ways to provide relief for the problem of raw materials.

2. While it is appropriate to raise import taxes on foreign goods entering our country to achieve the purpose of prohibition through taxation and to conform to the policy of tariff protection, the raw materials that our industry urgently needs are those that cannot be produced domestically and must be imported from abroad, such as fine serge and fine tweed. The government should exempt import taxes on raw materials to provide relief.

3. Currently, the import of foreign goods is initially subject to heavy import taxes by customs, followed by the payment of a considerable business tax by wholesalers, and then the payment of a second business tax by retailers. It is reported that our industry also bears the highest amount of business tax. If this is the case, our industry cannot imagine how to survive. The livelihoods of workers are difficult, and the government should devise ways to provide relief.

The above-mentioned points are related to the survival of our industry. Therefore, we should send a letter to your chamber of commerce to request that you forward it to the authorities concerned and quickly devise ways to provide relief.

Respectfully, Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce.

The Laundry Industry The Laundry Trade Association held an executive committee meeting yesterday, attended by more than ten committee members, chaired by Zhou Baotai. The resolutions were:

1. To hire Lawyer Kang as the association's permanent legal counsel. The resolution was passed and announced in the Shen Xin Min Guo three newspapers.

2. Regarding the case of a member, Fang Maoji, whose passenger and cargo were privately intercepted, causing disputes, how should it be handled? It was resolved to investigate and then review.

3. The new association premises have been leased at Fulu Lane, White Kerr Road, and a relocation should be scheduled. It was resolved to relocate on the 18th of this month, and a committee dinner will be held in the evening.

4. The Self-Defense Corps sent a letter requesting donations. It was resolved that each committee member would solicit donations.

The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Qian Chaofu Kidnapped This Morning

No News as of 3 O'Clock

Qian Chaofu, a native of Anting, aged 30, is the owner of Yongfeng Lumber Firm in the Lujiabang area of the South City Bund. Qian newly acquired a courtesan as a concubine named Yue'e. He kept her in a gilded cage at No. 27 Hehe Lane, Avenue Joffre in the French Concession. Qian had his own car, Concession number 1797, City number 1993. Every evening, Qian would take the car to his concubine's place, always returning late at night. This was his usual habit. Yesterday evening around 9 o'clock, Qian went as usual. It was not until 12:15 this morning that he was leaving her place. The chauffeur was starting the engine, heading east from Rue Bourgeat. As they approached the corner of Avenue de la Sape, just as they were about to turn south, four kidnappers suddenly jumped out from the roadside, brandishing pistols. They first forced the chauffeur out of the car. The kidnappers themselves drove off, taking Qian away without a trace. The chauffeur immediately rushed to inform Qian's concubine, who reported to the Songshan Road Police Station. The chief officer immediately ordered detectives to investigate. As of 3 o'clock this morning, the car had not been found.

Ye Jingsan's Account of Escaping Kidnapping

Treated Well During Captivity Released Calmly

Ye Jingsan, a tea merchant from Anhui Province, was kidnapped last Saturday morning while passing near the garbage bridge on North Suzhou Road by two bandits who forced him into a car. They drove to a remote location, where they robbed him of all the gold jewelry he had, worth about 90 taels, and held him captive for three days. Around 2 o'clock yesterday morning, he was led out by the bandits and walked for about four or five li before escaping. His losses amounted to several thousand dollars.

Traveling Between Shanghai and Hangzhou Ye Jingsan, aged 53, is a tea merchant residing at Shenyuan Tea Shop, No. 681 Jingxing Lane, North Henan Road, Public Concession. His younger brother owns Baocheng Silver Shop in Hangzhou. Recently, due to the high cost of gold and low cost of silver, he often entrusted Jingsan to sell gold jewelry at Wu Cangmin's Wanji Pawnshop on Avenue Edward VII to earn extra profit. On the 9th of this month, Ye received a letter from Hangzhou stating that there were gold ornaments for sale, so he took a train to Hangzhou that day and returned to Shanghai the next day.

Carrying Gold to Exchange Ye brought to Shanghai from Hangzhou this time, gold ornaments large and small, weighing about 89 taels. On the 11th, intending to go to Wanji Pawnshop on Avenue Edward VII to exchange them, he hid the gold ornaments on his person. Who knew that while passing near the old garbage bridge on the north side of the creek, two people suddenly caught up from behind and stopped Ye.

Kidnapped En Route Ye, seeing that the two men were behaving strangely, knew that he was encountering robbers and tried to turn around and escape. The two men dragged and twisted Ye away. After walking a few steps, they dragged him into a car that was parked on the side of the road, immediately started the engine, and sped away. At the same time, they blindfolded Ye with a cloth. After driving for about an hour, the bandits helped Ye out of the car and hid him in a small house. He was thoroughly searched, and all the cash he was carrying was robbed. (However, because he was blindfolded, he did not know the car number.) He was detained for three days and two nights, and the food and drink provided were fairly generous. Because someone was guarding him, his eyes were tightly covered with rubber tape. He did not know the address or any details about the house.

Shouting Loudly It was not until about 2 o'clock yesterday morning (the 14th), in the deep quiet of the night, that the bandits still blindfolded Ye and stuffed cotton wool into his mouth. Two bandits helped him out and walked for four or five li, tying Ye to a wooden electric pole. The limbs were tied tightly. The bandits then left. When the sky dawned, Ye spat out the cotton wool in his mouth and shouted for help. Soon, two women working in a straight factory passed by and saw it as a strange thing, not daring to approach. (That place is the Zhongshan Road area north of the Fanwangdu Creek in Western Shanghai.) They walked and talked, and when they reached the vicinity of Daxia University on Zhongshan Road, a police officer from the 2nd Security Team on guard duty heard about it, immediately went to the place, and indeed saw a person tied to a pole. He freed Ye and took him back to the team, asking him about what had happened. Unexpectedly, Ye had lost his mind and was mentally disturbed, seemingly losing consciousness, vaguely mumbling. Since there were no wounds on his body, Ye was released.

Reporting to the Police Station Ye staggered along the way and arrived at a bustling city, then hired a streetcar to return to the shop. After his thoughts gradually settled and he became a little clearer, he told the shop about the kidnapping and robbery. Afterwards, he personally reported the kidnapping and robbery to the Huisi Police Station in charge. After receiving the report, the chief officer questioned him in detail and at about 1 p.m. immediately dispatched a western detective and Chinese detectives Zhang Bingchen and Tan Haijin, etc., accompanied by Ye Jingsan, to the place of the kidnapping on Zhongshan Road by car to investigate. After confirming that the incident had occurred, they immediately took him back to the police station to await review. However, according to Ye, on the way to the hiding place from the kidnapping location, some roads were rugged and some were flat. He traveled a long distance, about two hours, so the hiding place was difficult to determine.

Female Student Ma Qiwen of Labor University Attempts Suicide by Taking Sleeping Pills

Ma Qiwen, a female student in the middle school department of Jiangwan National Labor University, suddenly took sleeping pills to commit suicide yesterday noon. Ms. Ma is 20 years old, a native of Yunnan, who came to Shanghai from afar to study at Labor University. She has been studying for three years and will soon graduate. Yesterday at 12:15 p.m., she swallowed a box of sleeping pill powder. The school authorities were extremely surprised when they heard the news and immediately ordered the school workers to first carry Ms. Ma on a canvas bed to the school doctor's office for treatment, and then hired a car to send her to Guangren Hospital. It was already 2:15 p.m. The female educator of the school, Ms. Liao Lianfang, registered her for special treatment. According to the doctor, the woman was initially unwilling to speak when she came to the hospital. After being persuaded by a female classmate who accompanied her, she finally told the truth that she had taken most of a bottle of sleeping pill powder. Fortunately, the drug was slow-acting, and most of it had been vomited out. Then, lavage and enema were used to inject the intestines and abdomen. One injection might save her life.

Verdict in Police Prosecution of Magic Troupe Case

Two Lus Sentenced to One Year Imprisonment Each

Zhao Huiying Sentenced to Six Months Imprisonment

Yu Huisheng's Bail Forfeited

The Spirit Magic Troupe organized by Lu Huilin and others invited women Chen Huifu and Wu Huirong, also known as Wu Aixian, to Tianjin to perform magic on December 13 of last year. When the troupe invited Chen and Wu to Tianjin, Wu Huirong joined privately without the consent of her parents. However, after the troupe arrived in Tianjin, Wu Huirong fell ill and died. When Lu Huilin and the other three returned to Shanghai, Wu's elder brother, Wu Caoyun, was ordered by his mother to negotiate with Lu and others at Room 303 of the Oriental Hotel. After several hours of negotiation, they failed to reach a resolution. Afterwards, Lu Huilin's father, Lu Zhengxiang, filed a complaint with the Laozha Police Station, accusing them of obstructing freedom and extortion, and the police arrested Wu Caoyun and Wu's relatives and friends, handing them over to the Special District Local Court. Xu Jiashi questioned them twice and sentenced Wu Caoyun and others to 30 days of detention and a fine of 200 yuan each. Wu and others refused to accept the verdict and appealed. During the hearing by Song, the presiding judge of the High Court, Lu and others stated that Wu Caoyun had not obstructed freedom or extorted money during the negotiations at the Oriental Hotel. Afterwards, Judge Song overturned the verdict, acquitted Wu Caoyun, and handed Lu Huilin, Zhao Huiying, Yu Huisheng, and Lu's father, Lu Zhengxiang, over to the police for investigation. The police considered that Lu and others were suspected of false accusation and enticement and filed a public prosecution. Zhou, the presiding judge of the Special District Local Court, held a hearing. The details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon at 2 o'clock, the third hearing was held. Additional witnesses were summoned and questioned. Only Yu Huisheng was absent from the defendants. After Judge Zhou questioned them, he allowed the lawyers of both parties to make their arguments. The prosecutor then stood up and argued that although Wu Huirong had signed a document with Lu and others when Lu Huilin and others invited Wu Huirong to Tianjin to perform magic, she did not have the consent of her parents, which constituted the crime of enticement under Article 257, which was not subject to discussion. As for the false accusation, Lu and others had confessed that Wu Caoyun had not obstructed freedom or extorted money during the negotiations at the Oriental Hotel. Although Lu and others later claimed that they changed their statements in the High Court because Wu Caoyun had asked someone to mediate, this was unreasonable. If Wu Caoyun had obstructed freedom and extorted money and the court had already ruled so, there was no reason to change their statements because the other party had requested mediation. The reason why Lu and others changed their statements was because their conscience was clear. Therefore, the crime of false accusation was also obvious. The court should judge the case according to law.

Judge Zhou then asked Lu and others if they had anything to say. Lu and others all replied no. Then, the verdict was announced as follows: Lu Zhengxiang is sentenced to one year imprisonment for the crime of false accusation. Lu Huilin is sentenced to one year imprisonment for the crime of enticing a woman under the age of 20. Zhao Huiying is sentenced to six months imprisonment for the crime of jointly enticing a woman under the age of 20. The trial procedure for Yu Huisheng is suspended, and his bail of 500 yuan is forfeited. During the appeal period, the two Lus were taken into custody. Zhao Huiying was released on bail of 500 yuan.

Creditors of Gongfa Company Dispose of Hot Spring Bathhouse and Chinese and Western Pharmacy

Relevant Parties Met at Zhongshe Yesterday

Methods Discussed for Disposing of Hot Spring Bathhouse

The Chinese and Western pharmacy and hot spring bathhouse operated by Huang Chu Jiu are both affiliated with Gongfa Company. Several months have passed since Huang's death, and there is no hope of repaying the debts owed by the two businesses. Recently, the creditors hired a lawyer to sue in the Special District Local Court and requested a preliminary attachment. The Special Court approved it. The bailiff and police were dispatched to seal the properties. At the bathhouse, the manager of the bathhouse, Yan Eson, arrived with a lawyer to negotiate with the creditors, requesting a delay in sealing. The creditors agreed to extend the deadline by one day, during which all the bathhouse's assets and furniture would be entrusted to the manager and other staff, who would be liable for compensation if there was any unauthorized removal or other issues. At the Chinese and Western pharmacy, lawyer Jiang Yiping negotiated with the creditors, Tu Jin'er, and accountants Pan and Wu, also agreeing to postpone the sealing. Because the deadline was very short, it was necessary to quickly find a solution. Therefore, yesterday (the 14th), the relevant parties met at the Zhongshe in Jing'an Temple to discuss solutions. Lawyers Wu Jingxiong, Chen Tingrui, and Jiang Yiping, as well as accountants Wu Zheng and Pan Zhaobang, and representatives of the creditors, attended the meeting. Lawyer Eson also represented the bathhouse manager.

The meeting first discussed the disposal of the hot spring bathhouse. After discussion, the creditors agreed to request the court to revoke the preliminary attachment so that the bathhouse could continue to operate. However, from then on, the creditors would send a representative to jointly manage the accounts with the bathhouse accountant on a daily basis, and all cash income would be deposited in the bank for safekeeping. This method was unanimously approved and passed. Then, they discussed the Chinese and Western pharmacy, and after much discussion, they did not immediately decide on a proper method. It was said that if it could be handled in the same way as the hot spring bathhouse, the creditors would probably not object.

Fire at Wanshou Temple in Pudong

The fire started from the west side of the main hall.

The idols in the center remain standing.

Wanshou Temple, located behind the Xiaoyangjing Temple at the eastern end of Lan Nidu in Pudong, was unfortunately destroyed by fire yesterday morning due to carelessness. Two main halls were burned down, and one was partially demolished. There are rumors that a junior monk started the fire out of revenge, but this has not been confirmed. The following is a record of the investigation:

History of the Temple: The temple is located behind the Xiaoyangjing Temple at the eastern end of the third district of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, covering an area of approximately two mu. It has a history of just over ten years since its construction. A monk named Benlai (approximately fifty years old) from Mount Putuo in Ningbo painstakingly raised funds from local devout men and women, taking three years to complete. It consists of three main halls facing south. The central hall houses over a dozen idols. The east hall is the monk's bedroom. There are three side rooms facing west, the central one also housing a large full-body Buddha statue. The north room is the incense caretaker's bedroom, and the south room stores miscellaneous items. Before the National Revolutionary Army arrived in Shanghai, the temple's incense offerings were quite prosperous in all four seasons, and the abbot's income was ample. After the establishment of the municipal government, due to the crackdown on temples and the elimination of superstition, those burning incense gradually disappeared. The desolate scene of late is a stark contrast to the past.

Origin of the Fire: The abbot, Benlai, lacking income, set off on the eighth of this month for Mount Putuo in Ningbo to offer incense. He locked his bedroom, leaving only the incense caretaker, Yuan Lianyou, to guard the temple. Yuan was timid, so he invited a beggar named Chen Alin to sleep in the side room at night for company. Last night, the two went to bed after eight o'clock. Unexpectedly, at half past one yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out in the west side room of the main hall, quickly becoming uncontrollable. The patrol police at the gate of the third district immediately sounded the alarm. District Chief Zhang immediately supervised all the police officers, each carrying basins and small buckets to fetch water from the Xiaobang River to douse the flames. At the same time, the east side room of the main hall was demolished to cut off the fire line. The Pudong fire brigade also arrived and started extinguishing the fire. After about an hour of burning, the fire gradually weakened and was finally extinguished. Two main halls were burned down. Most strangely, the many idols enshrined in the center remained standing, and their silk clothing was not damaged at all. Those who came to see it yesterday were amazed.

What About the Junior Monk? Afterwards, District Chief Zhang ordered the police to bring the incense caretaker, Yuan Lianyou, and the beggar, Lu Alin, to the district office for questioning about the cause of the fire. Yuan, fifty years old and from Ningbo, stated that he cooked meals in the temple but did not know where the fire came from. However, it was discovered that a junior monk named Longshan, eighteen years old, had brought a woman to the temple in late December of the lunar calendar last year and did not leave at night. Benlai found them and questioned them. Longshan instead beat Benlai, so he reported the incident to the police, who sent Longshan to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. Later, after Longshan was released, he tried to return to the temple, but Benlai drove him away. The two had a feud. It is unknown whether this fire was set by him as an act of revenge. The district chief then ordered the police to issue a summons for Longshan, but he could not be found. Lu Alin was deemed unrelated and released. Yuan Lianyou was escorted to the main bureau in the afternoon for further action. As no one was in charge of the temple, police officers were assigned to take turns guarding it to prevent theft.

Smuggling Company of Thieves

Using the "suffocation chamber" method

On an extremely large scale

The Lujiazui Water Police Station received multiple reports from the Shanghai Steamship Company stating that three boxes of Zhigong woolen fabric and two boxes of Huada woolen fabric had been stolen from the Changjiang steamer on January 8. The Tianxiang Foreign Firm reported that eleven boxes of rayon had been stolen from the Gehuasi steamer on February 6. The Yitai Company reported that seven boxes of Western feathered silk had been stolen from the Xierwupaimei steamer on March 14, worth thousands of gold coins. These were all large-scale thefts. The station ordered detectives Ge Changsheng, Cheng Yongnian, Huang Songsheng, and others to investigate. The detectives discovered that the method used in these thefts involved taking advantage of the chaos when cargo was being loaded onto the steamer to sneak into the cargo hold. After the workers finished their work and the hatch was tightly closed, the thieves believed no one could enter. Then, when the night was still and quiet, the gang hired a boat to moor alongside the steamer outside the hold and knocked on it with a secret code. The thieves inside the hold would open the hatch and steal the goods together. If they were not hiding inside the hold beforehand, those outside would not have the keys and would be unable to enter. This type of operation was called "suffocation chamber." Furthermore, this gang had organized a large-scale theft company, where all internal and external theft work was assigned by the leaders. The ringleaders were Yan Shirong, Zhang Xiaolian, Chen Erbian, Li Jinyu, and Wang Hongxi. Their theft company was located at a teahouse opened by Yan Shirong at the intersection of Wuzhou Road and Youheng Road. After the detectives investigated and confirmed this, they immediately made arrests in different locations. They apprehended thieves Chen Xiaowuzi, Wu Nailian, and Dou Xiaochezi. The others had already fled. They were taken to the Water Police Station, where Head Detective He interrogated them. The three confessed to the aforementioned weaving and theft methods. In addition to continuing to apprehend the remaining criminals, the three criminals were transferred to the local court for trial.

Pretending to Use Postal Car to Transport Opium

Caught by French Concession's Western Detective

Local Postal Authorities Thoroughly Investigate

A bag of opium, weighing 300 ounces, was seized. However, the car managed to escape with the remaining two bags. The local postal authorities, believing that postal cars are not subject to inspection as a matter of course, and that the nature of this case is serious, ordered a thorough investigation on Monday. According to the police report, the car was registered with the concession as No. 15436 and with the municipal government as No. 3178. It arrived at the Taikoo Wharf at about 2 pm on that afternoon. At that time, the Wusong wheel had been docked for half an hour, and several postal cars had just loaded a large number of mails and left. Therefore, the Western detective became suspicious and secretly paid attention. Later, he saw the car stop and start in the pier three times. Finally, three bags were sent from the ship to the car. When two bags were loaded into the car, the detective hurriedly opened the third bag and found that the bag was full of opium. Just as he was about to check the remaining two bags, the driver jumped into the car and drove away quickly into the Public Concession. It is now expected that this car must be a local opium smuggling organization posing as a postal car to avoid inspection.

Attempted Murder

Huang Changgen Allows Woman to Remarry

Ms. Fang Breaks Agreement and Suffers from Society

Huang Changgen from Ningbo previously married Ms. Fang from the same hometown. Later, because she was unfaithful and became acquainted with someone surnamed Yang, Huang dissolved their marriage, and Ms. Fang compensated Huang with one hundred gold. Huang agreed to let her remarry, but forbade her from marrying Mr. Yang. They signed a divorce agreement. Later, Ms. Fang only paid Huang sixty-five yuan and actually lived with Mr. Yang. Recently, Huang found out about this and was furious that Ms. Fang had broken the agreement. He decided to punish her to vent his anger. Knowing that she would definitely go to the Aierjin Road vegetable market every morning to buy vegetables, he waited near the vegetable market on the morning of the tenth of last month, carrying a sharp axe. He saw Ms. Fang passing by with a basket. Huang suddenly jumped out and砍er head with the axe, causing her to fall to the ground instantly. The patrol officer heard the alarm and arrived, arrested Huang, and sent him to the Special District Local Court. After Judge Ge concluded the trial, he announced the verdict yesterday afternoon: Huang Changgen attempted murder and was sentenced to seven years in prison, and the axe was confiscated.

Follow-up on Jufeng Wheel's Huge Theft Case

Discovery of Two Missing Boxes of Quinine

When the Jufeng Wheel previously sailed from Shanghai to Tianjin, 67 pieces of ramie cloth and one box of rayon silk were stolen. The Huishan Police Station recovered 63 pieces and 21 bolts of ramie cloth a few days ago. The comprador of the boat was notified to retrieve the goods. Three pieces (totaling 39 bolts) and one box of silk are still missing. This has already been reported in the previous reports. Yesterday, Jardine Matheson received a telegram from the Jufeng Wheel from Tianjin stating that two boxes of Western medicine quinine, worth about 1,100 taels of silver, were also found to be missing in the insured cabin when unloading goods in Tianjin. The goods are believed to have been stolen at the same time as the ramie cloth. After receiving the telegram, Jardine Matheson immediately informed the police station to rigorously investigate.

Verdict on Case of Man and Woman Carrying Opium

Sentenced to One Year of Imprisonment and a Fine

The day before yesterday night, a man and woman were traveling from south to north in separate rickshaws, passing the intersection of Xizang Road and Fuzhou Road. A patrol officer checked them and found two paper packages containing opium in the woman's rickshaw. Seeing that they had been caught, the man ordered the rickshaw driver to flee quickly, but he was caught and brought to the Laozha Police Station. It was learned that the woman was Zhu Xu and the man's name was Li Yongkang. According to the rickshaw driver, they boarded the rickshaw from the French Concession, and the opium was given to the woman by the man. They were sent to the Special District Local Court yesterday morning. Judge Zhou presided over the trial. The woman stated that the package was entrusted to her by someone else, and she did not initially know that it contained opium. Li's statement was evasive. The police lawyer, Ru Baoyi, requested that they be severely punished in accordance with the anti-smoking law. Judge Zhou immediately announced the verdict, sentencing each to one year of imprisonment and a fine of 140 yuan. The opium was confiscated.

Variety Show at the General Assembly of the Women's Temperance Association

In addition to various reports, speeches, and discussions, the Chinese Women's Temperance Association will also hold a variety show at the Central Assembly Hall on the evening of May 16 (Saturday). This event is elegant in nature. In addition to music, singing, and Peking opera, there will also be a new drama, "A Dream of Treasures," performed by students from Shanghai University. It is said that this play is a masterpiece by Liu Wang Liming of the Association, with a bizarre plot and profound meaning. Tickets are priced from one yuan to five yuan. All income will be used for the expenses of the Association's established educational institution.

Uniform Price for Kerosene Industry

Punishment for Violators

The Kerosene Industry Association of this city previously stipulated new prices due to repeated price increases of kerosene, which have been implemented since March 1. More than a month has passed since then, and abuses are inevitable. Recently, it has been heard that several companies are selling at extremely low prices, causing market chaos. The Association convened an emergency meeting a few days ago and strictly ordered all members to abide by the Association's charter and not to change the selling price privately. Those who dare to deliberately violate the rules will be punished in accordance with the rules. A notice was issued yesterday stating, "To all members, (omitted above) This time, most of the violations are excusable. Therefore, the first offense should not be punished. It has been decided that starting from the 12th of this month, low prices and scheduled deliveries will no longer be allowed. If anyone dares to continue to sell at low prices and make scheduled deliveries, they will be fined one yuan per box once discovered. If the invoice states the new price but secretly deducts commission, they will be fined two yuan per box." In addition to publishing the announcement in the newspaper, it is also recorded for your information, and you are required to comply. It is heard that since the 12th, old-brand boxed oil is sold for 11.25, bulk oil is sold for 11.05, new-brand cans are sold for 10.85, and old-brand cans are sold for 10.65 yuan. Baoyuan boxed oil is 11.25, the same price as Red Star. Guanghua new cans are 10.85, old cans are 10.65, and the same for Mei Da. It has been sold according to the price listed by the Association.

Wu Kerun's Home Robbed of Public Bonds

Report to Police for Record, Public Statement

Wu Kerun, styled Yucang, from JiangSu, currently the Director of General Affairs of the Hanyang Arsenal in Hubei, opened a residence in Shanghai at No. 62 Xinxin Lane, Jin Shenfu Road, in the French Concession. Unexpectedly, at noon on the 4th of this month, a large number of robbers suddenly invaded Wu's home and robbed them. In addition to the loss of clothing, jewelry, and silver dollars, they also robbed ten thousand yuan of demobilization public bonds with the following numbers: Nos. 001329 to 0013900, and 0015406 to 0015510. Mr. Wu has just learned about this after arriving in Shanghai from Hubei and has reported the situation to the French Police Station for the record yesterday. He has also issued a public statement in the newspaper stating,

Funeral of Madam Zhou, Mother of Dan

Madam Zhou, mother of artist Dan Duyu, managed her household with thrift and taught her children with principle. She was virtuous, kind, gentle, and respectful, a model for women. She passed away on the eleventh of this month. The funeral was held yesterday, and she was buried in the Shanghai Cemetery in Jiangwan. The water police team from Beixinjing Xiasha, the local defense corps, as well as friendly relatives, all came to pull the mourning rope. The white horses and plain cars were extremely grand for a time.

Yisheng Rubber Factory Opens Second Factory

Grand Banquet Last Night with Over a Thousand Guests

The Arrow Drum brand rubber overshoes produced by the Yisheng Rubber Factory in this city are sturdy, glossy, beautiful, and comfortable to walk in. Compared to imported products that are known for their reputation, they certainly have a reputation for being superior. Known far and wide, they are called the Arrow Drum brand, which is a homophone for "strong and durable," which can be said to live up to its name. As a result, sales have increased dramatically. Although six to seven thousand pairs can be produced every day, the demand still exceeds supply. The factory is now preparing to set up a second factory on Binlang Road, which will be put into operation in a blink of an eye to increase production. The factory adheres to the principle of small profits and widespread distribution, strives for excellence, and hopes to develop in order to repay the enthusiasm and patriotism of all sectors of society. Last night, the factory held a banquet at the Da Zhonghua Hotel for its customers and members of the press. Over a thousand people attended, hosted by Tu Dianchen, Mao Yuting, and others from the factory. It was an extremely grand occasion.

Liwa Dance Troupe to Perform "Dance Fan"

European and American sound films, in order to showcase their greatness and richness to the public, must include innovative singing and dancing, and the audience who do not understand English are fascinated by them because of the greatness of their singing and dancing. Therefore, European and American sound films have gained influence in the Far East, and their singing and dancing interludes are a major reason. Recently, a giant in the film industry has brought together singing and dancing stars Wei Rongbo, Huanghun, Yin Yizhi, and others to form a special Liwa Dance Troupe. Its purpose is to create special singing and dancing talents to supply the film industry for the production of sound and dance films. This is also the meaning of ten years of preparation, to enable Chinese sound films to excel in singing and dancing and to be able to compete with European and American sound films, which is extremely beautiful. Currently, the troupe has rented a Western-style house at No. 7 Huayuanfang, Jin Shenfu Road, in the French Concession as a training center, recruiting more than eighty male and female members, all of whom are children from clean families who have received considerable education. All the facilities in the institute are very perfect. The instructors, in addition to Wei Rongbo and Huanghun, also include the famous Russian dancer Ms. Huidengsigan. Since its establishment, it has been nearly five months, and the dance dramas that have been rehearsed include "Youth," "Under the Pomegranate Skirt," and the film "Luoshen." They are all original and can evoke a sense of beauty. It is also heard that the troupe has also hired artists Ma Xuweibang and Hu Chaoguang to be in charge of the scenery. The scenery for the above-mentioned plays has been completed, and the color and painting are all surreal in the style of futurism. It is heard that the backbone of the troupe plans to perform in the city next month. At that time, the atmosphere of the singing and dancing world will show a new situation.

Recent News from the Plum Blossom Troupe

The Plum Blossom Troupe performed at Siming Chinese and other theaters in Xiamen for 17 days, and at the invitation of the Xiamen Zhongshan Hospital Mountaineering Donation Team, performed at Zhongshan Park for three days. Later, on the 9th of this month, with the introduction of Mr. Liang Youquan, manager of Xiamen Mingming Film Company, all members of the troupe, still led by Mr. Wei Yunmei and Cai Wenjin, went to Shantou and began performing at the New Stage on the 11th for about 7 days. Then, they will go to Chaozhou, Hong Kong, Guangzhou, and other places under contract.

District Chief You Cracks Down on Dance Halls

The Xinmei Dance Hall at the end of North Sichuan Road, which was established by Japanese man Oda Fumio, had already been ordered by the Municipal Public Security Bureau to register and was instructed not to exceed the specified hours of operation. However, the Japanese man was ostensibly compliant but actually refused to implement the order. District Chief You of the Fifth District Public Security Bureau believed that Oda Fumio's contempt for our country's laws was extremely hateful. If he was not dealt with seriously, it would not be enough to show authority. Therefore, he repeatedly summoned Oda to the bureau to impose heavy fines as a warning and ordered all the dancers to quickly register with the Public Security Bureau in order to enforce the law.

Coffin Theft Case Discovered in Yuepu

Su, the First Wife of Sheng Mingqiu

Sheng Mingqiu, a famous doctor in Wusong, opened the Tianfutang Pharmacy at the Chamber of Commerce. His first wife, Su, died of illness in the eleventh year of the Republic of China. The coffin was temporarily placed in the Meiyuan family cemetery west of Yuepu Town, but it was not buried. Therefore, the outside of the coffin was built with a brick frame. Unexpectedly, the coffin frame was completely destroyed by coffin thieves the night before last, and gold and silver jewelry were stolen. Most reprehensibly, the bones were discarded outside the coffin in a messy manner, causing the remains to be exposed in a bleak scene. After someone came to Song to report yesterday, Sheng sent personnel to inspect and immediately arranged for people to organize the bones and repair the coffin frame. He specially submitted a petition to the Baoshan County Government to severely investigate and punish the perpetrators.

Inauguration of the National Goods Factory Joint Association's Executive and Supervisory Committees

The Shanghai National Goods Factories Joint Association held the inauguration ceremony for its Executive and Supervisory Committee members yesterday and discussed various cases. More than 30 people attended. Lu Xingzhuang was elected as chairman. After the oath of office, five standing committee members were elected from among themselves: Gu Jiuru, Lu Xingzhuang, Ma Jisheng, Shen Mengshi, and Sun Jiren. Committee members for each department were publicly recommended: Jiang Zhonghe for economics, Wang Dongyuan for statistics, Fang Jiange for law, Pan Dechun for publicity, Zhang Zilian and Xi Guansheng for training, Mou Yueqiu for review, Cao Zhigong for documentation, Yang Xiao'an for investigation, and Fei Xiaochu for general affairs. Shao Daren and Xu Jutang were additionally appointed as supervisory committee members. Xi Guansheng was also requested to report on his recent trip to Japan to investigate commercial conditions, and Xiang Songmao reported on methods to improve factory unity.

Establishment of the Taxi Industry Association

The Shanghai Taxi Industry Association held its inaugural meeting yesterday. Zhou Xiangsheng served as interim chairman. The chairman delivered an opening speech, followed by Dong Guitao reporting on the association's progress. Then, Ruan Quanhong read the association's charter, which was unanimously approved. Li Songquan, Zhou Peifu, Guo Shiliang, Xue Daoqi, Gu Deguang, Zhou Xiangsheng, Wu Guansheng, Chen Gengcai, Fang Yuefang, Ruan Quanhong, and Kong Fankui were elected as the eleven executive committee members. Ding Ruiming, Du Tianfa, Yan Jinsong, Li Hongfu, and Tang Jingsheng were elected as the five alternate executive committee members. Qian Wenhao, Hu Pengjiu, and Zheng Chaodian were elected as the three supervisory committee members. Finally, all members took a group photo and dispersed.

Cai Luoying Lost and Awaiting Collection

Twelve-year-old from Pudong

Lin, the guard squad leader of the 30th post of the 1st section of the 1st District Public Security Bureau, found a girl of about ten years old around 11 PM the night before last. She was wearing a floral calico short shirt and pants, flesh-colored stockings, and floral calico shoes, lost in Caocang Alley, Nanhui Hall Street, Dongjiadu, in the South City. He immediately took her back to the station. When questioned by the station chief, she stated that her name was Cai Luoying, twelve years old, from Pudong, and currently residing with relatives. Today, relatives accompanied her to return home, but she got separated on the way, resulting in her getting lost. She was instructed to stay temporarily, awaiting her family members to come to the station to claim her.

The Third Collection of "Saturday" Is Now on Sale

The third collection of "Saturday", renowned for its elegance and beauty, has now been bound and completed. The cover is exceptionally classic, and the content consists mostly of works by famous authors, full of aesthetic appeal. There are over three hundred photographs. Sales will begin today, with a price of one dollar and twenty cents per volume, plus fifteen cents for postage. Subscribers can get it for just two dollars and twenty cents, postage included. The distributor is the "Saturday" newspaper office in Maijia Circle.

Order to Police to Cut Their Hair

Chen Xizeng, the Director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, recently discovered that many of the police officers in the various departments and teams under his command still have long hair. This is considered unsightly and inconsistent with public morals and discipline. Yesterday, he specifically instructed the leaders of the various district teams to strictly order all their officers with long hair to cut it off immediately. Inspections will be conducted by designated personnel on the 15th of this month (i.e., today), and no negligence or delay will be tolerated.

Fire on Park Road This Morning

At 1:25 AM this morning, a fire suddenly broke out at 680 Park Road due to negligence. The flames quickly spread. Fire brigades from various districts rushed to the scene, but the fire was not extinguished until 2:30 AM. The damage was substantial.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: The Yangtze River basin will be cloudy or foggy. There will be strong southerly to southeasterly winds over the Yellow Sea and East China Sea. There are large cyclones in the Bohai Sea, the Liaodong Peninsula, and northern Korea. South of Zhejiang, the wind is unstable, with occasional fog and rain. Also, in the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 63.0 degrees, and the lowest was 50.9 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 55.2 degrees, and the lowest was 50.9 degrees.
