Letter to the Editor

To the Editor: Regarding the report in the local news section of your paper on the 12th about the strike by female workers in our factory's tin packaging department, the reports are slightly inaccurate. Our factory pays close attention to the treatment and work of our female workers. The cause of this strike was that a small number of female workers in the tin packaging department were performing poorly, affecting the quality of our products, and arbitrarily wasting materials used in the factory. Despite repeated warnings from our factory, they did not listen, and we had no choice but to dismiss them to restore order. However, these dismissed female workers used this as an excuse to incite the other well-behaved female workers to strike and cause disruptions starting on the 8th. They also seized the factory gate, threatening other female workers and preventing them from entering the factory to work. Our factory believes that these female workers' actions violated the law and immediately provided various forms of guidance and issued a notice ordering them to return to work as usual. Therefore, since the 10th, all the female workers have returned to the factory and are working as usual. As for the reported injuries to female workers and the withholding of wages, these are not true and can be easily investigated. Furthermore, our factory has not received the six demands that the female workers are said to have made, which is another misunderstanding. Our factory is deeply concerned that the public may not understand the truth of this strike, so we are making the above statement and requesting that you publish it in the "Letters to the Editor" section. We would be most grateful. Sincerely, Shanghai Sanxing Tobacco Company, April 13th.

Automobile News

Translated Compilation

Sino-French Joint Academic Expedition

— Xu

▲Date and Location of Departure: The Sino-French Joint Academic Expedition, comprised of twenty members and sponsored on the French side by Mr. Citroën, the General Manager of the Citroën Automobile Factory, will assemble on March 1st at the town of Périgueux, the officially agreed-upon departure point. The expedition will be led by explorer Mr. Haardt, the Commercial Director of the Citroën company, and Mr. Audouin-Dubreuil. Its objective is to traverse Central Asia.

▲One of the Collaborative Groups: This expedition has been two years in the making, and its scale is truly grand. It has received support from the French Geographical Society, the Museum of Natural History, the Ethnological Society, the Guimet Museum, and various other public academic organizations, making its organization even more comprehensive. It can be regarded as an unprecedented undertaking. Notably, the globally renowned U.S. National Geographic Society, with its 1.2 million members, has never before participated in any nation's academic expeditions since 1888. This time, it has changed its longstanding policy and will also collaborate with the expedition. As with naval officer Bellot's exploration of the Antarctic two years ago, Mr. Maynard was sent on behalf of the society to participate in the expedition.

▲Chinese Science to Be Revealed: The Chinese National Government and the Chinese Geographical Society will also take this opportunity to showcase their scientific work. Dr. Chu Minyi and five other scholars will follow the expedition and organize a Chinese academic expedition within China to continue the work of the French expedition.

▲A Talented and Diverse Team: The expedition staff consists of over forty individuals, comprising a mix of scholars, artists, and specialists. Accompanying Messrs. Haardt and Audouin-Dubreuil are several former French navy lieutenants specializing in surveying, secretary Mr. Gorges, Father Teilhard de Chardin specializing in archeology, zoology, and geology, painter Mr. Chekolev, Director of the Guimet Museum Mr. Hackin, zoologist Mr. Reymond, medical doctor Mr. Talaszto, and Messrs. Jouliaud, Benoist, and others.

▲Producing a Historical Travel Film: The expedition also has a film crew, led by film expert Mr. Sauvageot, with Messrs. Spek and Martial as deputies. They will exert their photographic artistry to produce a historical travel film of the expedition. Two empty trucks are available specifically for transporting camera equipment and sound recording devices. This crew will not only film previously unfilmed scenes of Asia but will also collect various sounds, such as songs, music, crowd noises, and natural sounds, to create an unprecedented and genuinely natural sound film masterpiece.

▲Citroën Vehicles for the Expedition: The expedition will use a total of thirteen vehicles, including seven six-cylinder climbing cars with trailers and six light vehicles, all supplied by the Citroën Automobile Factory and personally equipped by automobile engineer Mr. Kegresse. Two of these vehicles are exclusively for the expedition's science team, and two are for the sound and silent film crews. The medical room and kitchen also occupy two vehicles. The light vehicles will specialize in exploring high reefs and rugged roads and are equipped with a new hydraulic press. Their engines can withstand temperatures above 45 degrees Celsius and below 35 degrees Celsius.

▲Expert Arrangements Show Skill: All the vehicles are painted white with elegant horizontal stripes. The interiors have been arranged by experts to be extremely comfortable, ensuring that the accompanying personnel do not have to sleep on hard boards. Breakfast and rest can be enjoyed under open-air tents. These tents are handmade by experts and are extremely easy to assemble and disassemble, requiring only five minutes. Even in the difficult-to-travel Asia, the expedition will not feel any hardship. This shows the completeness of the expedition's organization.

▲Admirable Travel Determination: As for the expedition's route, Périgueux, Beijing, and Saigon will serve as assembly points. Even extremely difficult-to-travel terrain and extremely harsh climates between Manchuria and Siberia, such as the Gobi Desert and Chinese Turkestan, will be traversed by the expedition. Their indomitable determination and spirit of moving forward are truly admirable.

▲French President's Encouraging Words: Despite his busy schedule, French President Doumergue was intrigued and visited the expedition to meet the members and inspect all the expedition materials. Mr. Citroën, the General Manager of the Citroën Automobile Factory, and Mr. Haardt, the Commercial Director of Citroën and leader of the expedition, served as hosts. The French President studied the expedition's travel route in detail and spent over an hour explaining it to the various members of the expedition. He also praised the expedition's various regulations, such as the collaboration methods, financial management, and organizational details. He then inspected the final storage area for the expedition's materials before returning to the Presidential Palace. Upon departure, he expressed his most sincere wishes and words of encouragement to the members.

▲Sino-French Expedition to Meet in Xinjiang: It is said that the Chinese academic expedition will travel from Beijing to Kashgar, Xinjiang, to meet the French academic expedition led by Mr. Haardt. Thus, the so-called Sino-French Joint Academic Expedition will finally be formed. From there, they will travel together to the Gobi Desert, passing through Chinese Turkestan.
